## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: materials science / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature constitutive relationship of a material. Stress depends on strain through elastic/plastic laws, while temperature modulates material stiffness, yield strength, and flow behavior through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's Law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's Law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (elastic modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain curve, Ramberg-Osgood type)
- Johnson-Cook type (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (combined power-law hardening and thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (Arrhenius-like thermal activation of modulus)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Hollomon with thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal dependence)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (polynomial constitutive law)
- Neo-Hookean hyperelastic: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**2) * (c2 + c3 * T) (rubber-like elasticity with temperature)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 - c4 * T) (shifted power law with thermal softening)
- Rational thermal modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * c1 / (c2 + T) (modulus with inverse temperature dependence)
- Bilinear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon**2 (elastic-plastic transition approximation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening in metals → multiplicative factor (1 - T/T_melt) or (T_ref - T) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form representing dislocation density saturation
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**n with 0 < n < 1 representing work hardening in metals
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(-c/T) or exp(c*T) for thermally activated deformation processes
- Shifted power law (Swift) → (epsilon + epsilon_0)**n to avoid singularity at zero strain
- Modulus-temperature coupling → E(T) as a separate multiplicative function, often linear or exponential in T
- Yield stress offset → additive constant c0 representing initial yield before hardening (sigma_y + f(epsilon))
- Rubber elasticity temperature stiffening → stress proportional to T (entropic elasticity, opposite to metals)
